тАШрдкреНрд░ рдпрджреНрд╡рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖рдЯреНрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рджреГрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдХреГрдгреНрд╡рдЧреЛрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдкреБрдирд░реНрд╡рддреНрд╕рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдВ рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░рдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ – рдкреНрд░ рдпрджреНрд╡рдГ рд╖рдЯреНрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдкреБрдирд░реНрд╡рддреНрд╕реЛ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡реНрдпреВрд│реНрд╣реЗ рджрд╢рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рдкреНрд░рдердореЗ рдЫрдиреНрджреЛрдо рдЖрдЧреНрдирд┐рдорд╛рд░реБрддрд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░ рдЗрджрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдирдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ - рдкреНрд░ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдВ рджреВрддрдВ рд╡ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдорд╛рд░реБрддрдореН ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рео. реп) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

+Jamison Brereton

7 (627)
Maruts
Punarvatsa K─Бс╣Зva
36 verses: g─Бyatr─л
Although a tr╠еca division is possible for this hymn, it does not impose itself. This is one of only three Marut hymns in VIII (with VIII.20 and VIII.94). As with most Marut hymns, this one contains considerable description of the effects on the cosmos of these embodiments of storm and of their journey through the midspace: the bowing of the mountains, the violent winds and rain, the roaring. These descriptions are found primarily in the first part of the hymn (e.g., vss. 2тАУ5, 7тАУ8) and toward the end (see esp. vs. 34, with its bowing mountains forming a ring with vss. 2 and 5). The middle portion of the hymn (approximately vss. 11тАУ21) expresses our desires for their presence at our sac rifice and for their gifts, with the last two verses (20тАУ21) posing anxious ques
tions concerning the whereabouts of the Maruts and the loss of their attention. This anxiety returns in two further question verses, 30тАУ31, which preface the MarutsтАЩ final journey to the place of sacrifice, where they are praised together with Agni (vss. 32тАУ26).
Verses 22тАУ26 present various fragments of mythology; particularly striking, and baffling, is verse 26 with its mention of the poet U┼Ыan─Б and the тАЬloins of the ox,тАЭ which may be a glancing reference to the Vala cave.
Like other long hymns in VIII the structure of this one is quite loose. However, it does have at least a sketchy ring: in addition to verses 2/5 and 34 mentioned above, note the references to meter in the first and last verses (1 and 36). It is char acterized also by recycling of vocabulary, by rhetorical repetition (see, e.g., vss. 6, 9, 17, 22тАУ24), and by frequent phonetic figures (a particularly nice one is found in 28ab:…pr╠е╠Бс╣гat─л ra╠Бthe / pra╠Бс╣гс╣нir…ro╠Бhitaс╕е).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Maruts As noted in the published introduction, this hymn contains dense repetitions of vocabulary and numerous phonetic echoes within and across verses. I have noted some, but by no means all, below. Particularly common in the earlier part of the hymn is the root тИЪy─Б тАШdriveтАЩ, in both verbal and nominal forms (2b, 4c [2x], 5a, 7b, 8b; also 14b, 23a, 26b, 28c, 29c).

рд╣реЗ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рдорд┐рддрд░рд╛рд╡рд┐рдгреЛ рдорд┐рддрд░реЛрдЪрд┐рдиреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдПрддрддреНрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдордХрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рдЧрдгрд╛рдГред рдкрд╛рджрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН тАШ рдЕрдкрд╛рджрд╛рджреМ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрд░реНрдпреБрджрд╛рд╕рд╛рджрд╛рд╖реНрдЯрдорд┐рдХрдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрд╛рднрд╛рд╡реЗ рд╖рд╛рд╖реНрдард┐рдХрдорд╛рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд┐рддрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рдГ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡реА рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБ рд╕рд╡рдиреЗрд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╡реИрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд╛ рд╕рдВрдмрджреНрдзрд╛рдВ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрджрд┐рдирд╕рд╡рдирд┐рдХреАрдореН рдЗрд╖рдВ рд╕реЛрдорд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдордиреНрдирдВ рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рдкреНрд░ рдЕрдХреНрд╖рд░рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╕рд┐рдЮреНрдЪрддреН рдЕрдЧреНрдиреМ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкрддреН ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдВ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдХрдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдорд┐рд╖рдВ рд╕реЛрдордВ рдЪреЗрддрд┐ рдпреЛрдЬреНрдпрдореН ред рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддреЗрд╖реБ рдкрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреНрд╕реБ рд╢рд┐рд▓реЛрдЪреНрдЪрдпреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд┐ рд░рд╛рдЬрде ред рддреЗрди рд╕реЛрдореЗрди рд▓рдмреНрдзрдмрд▓рд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рджреАрдкреНрддрд╛ рднрд╡рде рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen the pious worshipper offers you, Maruts, food at the three diurnal rites, then you havesovereignty over the mountains.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Food at the three diurnal rites: triс╣гс╣нubham iс╣гam: chief at the three dailylibations, triс╣гu savaneс╣гu pra┼Ыasyam; praised by the three deities, tribhir devaiс╕е stutam; accompanied by hymnsin the triс╣гс╣нubh metre, i.e., the Soma offering at the mid-day libation

+Jamison Brereton

In that the inspired poet has let flow the triс╣гс╣нubh refreshment to you, o Maruts,
you rule [/shine] throughout the mountains.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

(Indra), a hymn that is also not in Triс╣гс╣нubh. Some remove the word here entirely from the poetic sphere, as in MacdonellтАЩs тАЬthreefold Soma draught.тАЭ Geldner believes that it canтАЩt refer to the Triс╣гс╣нubh meter here, but that it must be a different technical term in recitation. I do not think that the fact that these two hymns are not in Triс╣гс╣нubh necessarily means that that meter canтАЩt be referred to in this expression; there are, after all, plenty of hymns to both the Maruts and Indra in Triс╣гс╣нubh, and the verb governing the phrase is in the imperfect and therefore should refer to another occasion. But following GeldnerтАЩs lead, I think it possible that тАШ(having?) threefold rhythmтАЩ could refer to the G─Бyatr─л meter in which this hymn is composed, since G─Бyatr─л consists of three p─Бdas. Unfortunately this will not work for VIII.69, which is composed in a variety of meters (incl. G─Бyatr─л, but only vss. 4-6); the verse in which the phrase is found (VIII.69.1) is in Anuс╣гс╣нubh. I might emend the published translation to тАЬrefreshment in threefold rhythm.тАЭ For further on the compound see Scarlatta (641-42), who is somewhat indecisive about both the compound type and the sense.

+Griffith

O MARUTS, when the sage hath poured the Trstup forth as food for you,
Ye shine amid the mountain-clouds.

+Macdonell

When, Maruts, now for you the sage Pours out the threefold Soma draught, Ye shine forth on the mountain heights.

+Geldner

Wenn der Redekundige f├╝r euch, Marut, den Tristubh-Ohrenschmaus ergossen hat, so f├╝hret ihr im Gebirge das Regiment;

+Grassmann

Wenn, Maruts, euch der S├дnger nun des Preisgesanges Trunk ergoss, So gl├дnzt ihr auf den Wolkenh├╢hn.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen, glorious and powerful (Maruts), you fit out your chariot, the mountains depart (from their plural ces).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Nyah─Бsata: from h─Б gatau, they move out of your way through fear

+Jamison Brereton

In that you have certainly set your attention on your course, you resplendent ones displaying your power,
the mountains have bent down.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

├бcidhvam in b (see also the identical p─Бda in 14b) should be read with distracted final syllable (├бcidhu vam) in order to make up an 8-syllable p─Бda, but it also should ideally have a heavy root syllable in order to avoid four consecutive light syllables in the cadence. (Even though I do not believe that the cadences of dimeter verse are as regulated as those in trimeter, iambic cadences do prevail, and four shorts would be quite unusual.) Werba (183, flg. Seebold) suggests that the form represents *├бcid-dhu vam to тИЪcit, which seems very plausible (also for the identical distracted form in I.87.2; in V.55.7 it does not require distraction and is therefore not diagnostic). Grassmann assigns ├бcidhvam to тИЪci, which is nearly identical in meaning to тИЪcit; Lubotsky, curiously, puts it with тИЪci тАШpileтАЩ. The same type of cluster reduction is found in the Marut hymn VIII.20.18 in vavс╣Ыdhu vam, which likewise requires distraction and a heavy root syllable and represents *vavс╣Ыd-dhu vam from тИЪvс╣Ыt тАШturnтАЩ.

+Grassmann

Als ihr o starke, gl├дnzende, nun eure Reise unternahmt, Da neigten sich die Berge euch.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe mountains are curbed, the rivers are restrained at your coming, for the upholding of your greatstrength.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Or, when the mountains are curbed at your coming, (and) the rivers are stayed for the sustaining ofyour great strength; for the upholding: vidharmaс╣Зe mahe ┼Ыuс╣гm─Бya yemire = vidharaс╣З─Бya mahateyuс╣гmad─лy─Бya bal─Бya svayam eva niyamyante. The mountains and rivers are of their own accord restrainedfor sustaining your great strength; they abide ogether in one plural ce through fear of our coming and strength,yuс╣гmad y─Бm─Бd bal─Бcca bh─лty─Б ekatraikasth─Бne niyat─Б vartante

+Jamison Brereton

When the mountain peak (holds itself) down for your coursing, and the rivers hold themselves down for your expansion and for your great gusting.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. consists only of a subordinate clause. I attach it to the preceding vs., since the y├бd clause of 4c seems parallel to the y├бd clause of 5 and y─Б╠Бma- recurs here.

However, there is a change from 3rd ps. ref. in 4 to 2nd ps. in 5.

So to sustain your mighty force.

+Macdonell

+Geldner

Wenn das Gebirge vor eurer Fahrt, die Fl├╝sse vor eurer Ausbreitung, vor eurem gro├Яen Ungest├╝m gewichen sind.

+Grassmann

Wenn Berge weichen eurem Gang und Str├╢me eurem Machtgebot, vor eurer allgewalt’gen Kraft.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey, who by their might open a radiant path for the sun to travel, they pervade (the world) with lustre.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

They release the rein [/ray] with strength, for the sun to travel its path; they have extended themselves with its radiant beams.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Exactly what atmospheric phenomenon is being described here is not clear.

Geldner seems to think that itтАЩs the Maruts who are traveling the path (p├бnth─Бm тАж y─Б╠Бtave тАЬdass sie ihre Bahn laufeтАЭ), though his n. 8b seems closer to my interpr. I suggest that it is a post-storm image: the thunderclouds/Maruts part, releasing the sunтАЩs ray and allowing the sun to travel its usual path across the sky. The parting of the clouds is expressed in c, the extending or spreading of the clouds that is accompanied by the beams of the sun. Thieme (Fremd. 112) instead sees the Maruts releasing a ray as the path for the sun to travel: the first ray of morning, which the sun follows. But the Maruts are not dawn gods.

P─Бda c is repeated as the final p─Бda of the hymn (36c).

+Griffith

With might they drop the loosened rein so that the Sun may run his course,
And spread themselves with beams of light.

+Macdonell

With power they shoot a ray of light So that the sun may run his course; They with their beams spread far and wide.

+Geldner

Sie lassen mit Macht der Sonne den Z├╝gel schie├Яen, da├Я sie ihre Bahn laufe. Zugleich mit deren Strahlen haben sie sich zerstreut.

+Grassmann

Sie werfen kr├дftig ihre Schnur, der Sonne Pfad zu messen, aus; Mit Strahlen breiten sie sich aus.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe kine have filled for the thunderer three lakes of the sweet (Soma) from the dripping water-bearingcloud.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Kine: pс╣Ы┼Ыnayaс╕е, the cows, the mothers of the Maruts: marunm─Бtс╣Ы bh┼лt─Б g─Бvaс╕е; or, the sons ofPс╣Ы┼Ыni, the Maruts; or, the hymns at the mid-day libation being recited in a middle tone: m─Бdhyamik─Б v─Бcaс╕е;three lakes: libations of milk, etc., mixed with the Soma at the three diurnal rrites; or libations of Soma filling thethree vessels: droс╣Зakala┼Ыa, ─Бhavan─лya and p┼лtabhс╣Ыt; dripping water-bearing cloud: utsam kabandhamudriс╣Зam = utsravaс╣Зa┼Ы─лlam, exuding, dropping;

Udakam = water; udriс╣Зam udakavantam megham, havingwater, a cloud; they have milked the dripping water from the cloud

+Jamison Brereton

Three lakes did the dappled ones milk out as honey for the mace-bearer, a wellspring, a cask full of water.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The stem pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыni- in the plural otherwise refers to тАЬdappled cowsтАЭ and is marked (by pronouns and modifying adjectives) as feminine; see the immediate preceding hymn VIII.6.19, as well as VIII.69.3, I.84.11. Here, however, there are no diagnostically feminine forms syntactically associated with pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnayaс╕е. This allows it to refer both to (fem.) dappled cows and to the (masc.) Maruts, whose mother is Pс╣Ы┼Ыni. Although the Maruts are regularly called тАЬRudrasтАЭ after their father Rudra (e.g., 12b), this is the only place in the RV where they are called тАЬPс╣Ы┼ЫnisтАЭ after their mother. This verse reprises 3bc тАж pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnim─Бtaraс╕е / dhukс╣г├бnta pipy├║┼Ы─лm ├нс╣гam тАЬThey whose mother is Pr┼Ы╠е ni have milked out swelling refreshment,тАЭ with the bahuvr─лhi pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnim─Бtaraс╕е matched with pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnayaс╕е here and dhukс╣г├бnta matching duduhr├й. The pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnim─Бtaraс╕е in 3b all but ensures that we will take pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnayaс╕е here as a referent to the Maruts.

The referent of the three lakes they milk out as honey is the rain they produce.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMunificent, mighty Rudras, you in the sacrificial hall are wise (even) in the exhilaration (of the Soma).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mighty Rudras: sons of Rudra, rudraputr─Бс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

ForтАФo Rudras, masters of the R╠еbhus, possessing good dropsтАФin our house
and also in exhilaration you are provident.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou (see his comm.) take sud─Бnavo, r├║dr─Б с╣Ыbhukс╣гaс╣Зaс╕е as predicative vocatives with the copula expression y┼лy├бс╣Г h├н с╣гс╣нh─Б╠БтАЬfor you are тАжтАЭ This seems unnecessary, since there is a fine nominative plural, pr├бcetasaс╕е, which can serve as predicate. I take the ut├б to be connecting not the supposed predicative vocc.

with pr├бcetasaс╕е, but the two locc. d├бme and m├бde. The predicative vocative analysis is esp. unlikely because this is a repeated p─Бda (I.15.2, VI.51.15, VIII.83.9; there are also further exx. of y┼лy├бm h├н с╣гс╣нh─Б╠БтАж as a p─Бda-opening), and only in I.15.2 is a predicative voc. likely. (See Bloomfield, Rig-Veda Repetitions ad I.15.2; he considers it тАЬplain mechanical borrowingтАЭ there.) The conjoined locc. тАЬin our house and in exhilarationтАЭ may not seem to form a natural semantic class, but note that they are anagrams of each other: d├бme / m├бde, and in a hymn so structured by phonetics, that would be enough.

+Griffith

Wise when the gladdening draught is drunk.

+Macdonell

+Geldner

Ihr seid ja die Gabensch├╢nen, ihr Rudra┬┤s, die Gebieter im Hause und auch im Somarausche bei Verstand.

+Grassmann

Denn ihr seid gabenreich im Haus, o Rudra’s, Ribhuherrscher ihr, Und achtsam bei dem Somatrunk.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

+Jamison Brereton

Wealth, arousing exhilaration, consisting of much livestock, all-nourishingтАФ
impel it here to us from heaven, o Maruts.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I take madacy├║tam as having тАЬactiveтАЭ meaning (тАШarousing exhilarationтАЩ), rather than passive. Scarlatta (126) allows either for this stem, and Renou takes it as passive here. Since the passive form m├бdacyutam built with the past participle would fit the same metrical slot, I think that the active sense must be meant.

mediopassive participle to тИЪsu тАШpressтАЩ (тАШbeing pressedтАЩ), which is eminently appropriate for drops, and a thematic adj. to тИЪsvan тАШsoundтАЩ. +Wilson
English translation:

тАЬA man should solicit happiness of them with praises of such an unconquerable (company).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A manshould: or, a man should solicit by his praises the happiness which belongs to them, to such an unconquerable(company)

+Jamison Brereton

A mortal might beg benevolence of them,
even of such an undeceivable (flock), with his prayers.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The problem in this verse is the referent and syntactic construction of gen. sg. et─Б╠Бvataс╕е тАж ├бd─Бbhyasya (assuming that the two are to be construed together).

Most take the phrase as obj., one way or another, of bhikс╣гeta. Geldner takes it as a separate obj. of bhikс╣гeta, parallel to sumn├бm: тАЬUm solche unfehlbare (Gabe), um ihre Gunst тАжтАЭ Oldenberg, by contrast, suggests that the poet started out with the gen. et─Б╠Бvataс╕е, meaning to continue with *sumn├бsya, but had to substitute the acc. sumn├бm for metrical reasons. He then takes ├бd─Бbhyasya either as continuing the gen. phrase et─Б╠Бvataс╕е тАж *sumn├бsya or as having a separate referent, the Maruts considered as a unity. Renou also considers sumn├б- to be the ultimate referent, but has the genitive phrase express a partitive sense: тАЬPuisse le mortel avoir une part, (si) petite (soit-elle), ├а la bonne grace тАжтАЭ Sim. Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions) ad loc. In favor of the Oldenberg/Renou/Bloomfield solution is the phrase et─Б╠Бvataс╕е тАж sumn├бsya in VIII.49.9 (V─Бlakh.), construed with ─лmahe тАШwe begтАЩ (cf. 50.9); see also VIII.5.27 et─Б╠Бvat… / … sumn├бm ─лmahe. But I find OldenbergтАЩs metrical about-face very unlikely: RVic poets donтАЩt have тАЬwhoops, that genitive wonтАЩt fit hereтАЭ compositional moments, as far as I can tell, while RenouтАЩs semi-partitive construction seems rather weaselly. Moreover, тИЪbhikс╣г is almost always construed with the acc. as here (genitives probably in I.152.6 and VII.90.6). And, further, in the scenario where ├бd─Бbhyasya is part of the phrase, тАЬunfehlbarтАЭ (Geldner), тАЬunerringтАЭ (Bloomfield) is not what ├бd─Бbhya- means. My solution is not necessarily better, though it does arise in part from OldenbergтАЩs alternative suggestion for ├бd─Бbhyasya. I take the gen. sg. phrase as doubling the gen. pl., eс╣г─Бm, with both referring to the Maruts – the plural to them individually, the singular to their collectivity (so OldenbergтАЩs тАЬvon den als Einheit gedachten MarutsтАЭ), i.e., the Marut flock (gaс╣З├б-). This seems to be GrassmannтАЩs view, also MacdonellтАЩs. It should be noted that the Maruts (in pl.) are several times referred to as ├бd─Бbhya- (II.34.10, III.26.4).

The published translation reflects that analysis, but I am not entirely certain it is right. If I were to follow some version of the other view, I would render bhikс╣гeta in two different ways depending on the case of its complement: тАЬmight beg their benevolence, might seek a share of such undeceivable …тАЭ

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey who, like dropping showers, inflate heaven and earth with rain, milking the inexhaustible cloud.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

They who, like droplets, blow their blast through the two world-halves along with their rains,
milking the unfailing wellspring,

+Jamison Brereton Notes

However odd the expression draps─Б╠Бс╕е тАж dh├бmanti тАЬthe droplets blow their blastтАЭ may seem, it is found twice elsewhere: the extremely enigmatic VIII.96.13 and the somewhat clearer IX.73.1. The latter is a noise-making context, as this may be.

+Griffith

They who like fiery sparks with showers of rain blow through the heaven and earth,
Milking the spring that never fails.

+Macdonell

They who, like sparks, with showers of rain, Blow onward through both heaven and earth, And milk the spring that never fails:

+Geldner

Die wie die Blasen werfenden Somatropfen beide Welten mit Regen beblasen, indem sie den unversiegbaren Quell melken.

+Grassmann

Sie, die den unersch├╢pften Born ergiessend alle Welt bespr├╝hn mit Regen wie der Tropfen Schwall,

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWe meditate on that (genitive rosity) whereby for (the sake of granting them) riches you have protectedTurva┼Ыa and Yadu and the wealth-desiring Kaс╣Зva.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

With which (aid) you aided Turva┼Ыa and Yadu, with which (you aided) Kaс╣Зva, who gained the stakes,
may we receive (a portion) of this for wealth.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the extremely recessive 2nd pl. perfect ─Бv├б: 2nd pl. pfs. are rare and poorly marked as it is; with its initial swallowed by y├йna, this one barely surfaces.

The referent of y├йna and its correlative t├бsya is most likely тАШhelpтАЩ (├бvas-); so Geldner This assumption is supported by I.112.5 y─Б╠Бbhiс╕е k├бс╣Зvam тАж ─Б╠Бvatam тАЬwith which you two helped Kaс╣Зva,тАЭ where the referent of y─Б╠Бbhiс╕е is the etymologically related ┼лt├нbhiс╕е and the same Kaс╣Зva story as in 18b is referred to.

As for Turva┼Ыa and Yadu – though, as Geldner points out, their helper is usually Indra, in this run of hymns the deed is assigned to several different gods: the Maruts (here), Indra (VIII.4.7), the A┼Ыvins (VIII.9.14, 10.5).

The construction of c is unusual. With Geldner (and Renou), I take t├бsya as a partitive gen. with dh─лmahi, though somewhat reluctantly. The dat. r─Бy├й тАШfor wealthтАЩ is then an indication of our purpose once we receive some help from the Maruts; GeldnerтАЩs fuller тАЬum Reichtum (zu gewinnen)тАЭ makes the purpose clearer.

+Griffith

For wealth, we think of that whereby ye aided Yadu, Turvasa,
And KanVa who obtained the spoil.

+Macdonell

For riches, let us surely win Your help that aided Turva┼Ыa, Yadu, Kaс╣Зva, who gained great wealth.

+Geldner

Womit ihr dem Turvasa und Yadu, womit ihr dem preisgewinnenden Kanva beigestanden habt, dieser Hilfe m├╢chten wir fein teilhaft werden um Reichtum zu gewinnen.

+Grassmann

Der Reichthum werde uns zu Theil mit dem ihr Turva├зa, Jadu Und Kanva’n halft, der Preis errang.

+Elizarenkova

What Brahman is adoring you?

+Macdonell

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(Maruts), for whom the sacred grass is trimmed, it cannot be (that you submit to be detained), for youhave derived strength from the sacrifice, formerly (accompanied) by our praises.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sacred grass: vс╣Ыkta barhiс╣гaс╕е(barhiriti yaj├▒an─Бma) = those by whom the grass has been trimmed, i.e. the priests; “It cannot be, for, priests,by your praises preceding (those of others) you have propitiated the energies of the Maruts, the objects of thesacrifice”; for you have derived strength: or, for by the former praises (of others) you have nourished strengthconnected with the sacrifice

+Jamison Brereton

For it is not (now) as it was before, when in return for our praises of you you used to animate the troops of truth, o you for whom the ritual
grass has been twisted.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner thinks that this verse is addressed to the other singers, but this requires that the voc. vrktabarhi ╠е с╣гaс╕е in 20 and 21 have two different referents (so explicitly GeldnerтАЩs n. 3), which seems unlikely. I take the Maruts to be the addressees, as in vs. 20, and follow Macdonell (Hymns from the Rigveda, p. 60) as well as L├╝ders (Var. 426- 27) in taking the verse as contrasting the MarutsтАЩ former friendly behavior to the poet and his fellow ritualists with their neglect now – a neglect drawn attention to by the questions in the immediately preceding vs. 20. Acdg. to Delbr├╝ck (AiS 502), ha sma pur─Б╠Б+ PRESENT expresses what was accustomed to happen in the past. I also take st├│mebhiс╕е not as the MarutsтАЩ praise songs, but rather the ones produced by us, as an instrumental of price. MacdonellтАЩs tr. тАЬas once ye did for praiseтАжтАЭ seems to reflect a similar interpr.

+Griffith

Is it not there where ye of old, supplied with sacred grass, for lauds
Inspired the strong in sacrifice?

+Macdonell

For ye, for whom the straw is spread. Do not, as once ye did for praise, Rejoice our sacrificers’ ranks.

+Geldner

Ist es denn nicht, da├Я ihr schon fr├╝her mit euren Lobges├дngen die Heerscharen des Gesetzes ermuntert habt, die ihr Barhis umleget?

+Grassmann

Denn ohne dass sie euch zuvor gepriesen auf geweihter Streu, Erquicket ihr des Opfers Schar.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

ar─Бj├нn- is a hapax. Though it is obviously derived from a root тИЪr─Бj, it is not clear whether it belongs to тАШshineтАЩ (so Grassmann тАШnicht gl├дnzendтАЩ, Renou тАШsans ├йclatтАЩ) or тАШruleтАЩ (Geldner тАШdie herrenlosen BergeтАЩ; Oldenberg тАШk├╢niglosтАЩ) – or both, as I suspect. Although neither root yields compelling sense as a negated quality of mountains, the phrase should be interpreted in light of 1c v├н p├бrvateс╣гu r─Бjatha, where I see the same pun.

It is possible that v├н тИЪy─Б should be rendered тАШdrive throughтАЩ, not тАШdrive apartтАЩ, although this produces a less happy contrast with s├бm in vs. 22. In that case I would tr. тАЬthey drove through Vс╣Ыtra, joint by joint, (drove) through the mountains тАжтАЭ On vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зi see comm. ad VIII.96.19.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey have come to the aid of the warring Trita, invigorating his strength, and (animating) his acts; theyhave come to the aid of Indra, for the destruction of Vс╣Ыtra.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

They stood by the unbridled force and the resolve of Trita, while he was fighting,
(stood) by Indra at the overcoming of Vr╠еtra.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The pattern of repeated preverbs continues with ├бnu. The lexeme ├бnu тИЪav is quite rare (but see X.113.1); presumably the poet was looking for a preverb to pattern with s├бm and v├н in the previous vss. In X.113.1 I tr. тАШassistтАЩ, but тАШstand byтАЩ here to provide a separable particle for the pattern.

+Griffith

They reinforced the power and strength of Trita as he fought, and helped
Indra in battle with the foe.

+Macdonell

They reinforced the mighty strength And skill of Trita as he fought, And Indra in the Vс╣Ыtra-fray.

+Geldner

Sie lie├Яen den Mut und die Umsicht des k├дmpfenden Trita, sie lie├Яen den Indra im Vritrakampf gew├дhren.

+Grassmann

Des Trita Kraft und Heldenmuth erfrischten in dem Kampfe sie, Den Indra in der Vritraschlacht.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe birlliant (Maruts), bearing the lightning in their hands, radiant above all, gloriously display theirgolden helmets on their heads.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

With lightning in their hands, heaven-boundтАФgolden (helmet-)lips (stretched out) on their headтАФ
the resplendent ones anointed themselves for beauty.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I have punctuated p─Бda b as a parenthetical expression, a nominal locational clause, but in context it is the equivalent of a decompounded bahuvr─лhi modifying the Maruts and parallel to vidy├║ddhast─Б(с╕е) тАШhaving lightning in their handsтАЩ in p─Бda a (so approx. Renou). A bahuvr─лhi would have been difficult to construct with these elements. Including the modifier тАШgoldenтАЩ would have produced a threemember compound, which would be unusual for the RV, and determining what form тАШheadтАЩ (┼Ы├нras- / ┼Ы─лс╣Ыс╣г-с╣З-) would have taken as the final member of a masc. pl.

bahuvr─лhi may have defeated the poet. This analytic expression is given somewhat fuller form in V.54.11.

+Griffith

They deck themselves for glory, bright, celestial, lightning in their hands,
And helms of gold upon their heads.

+Macdonell

Celestial, lightnings in their hands, They wear gold helmets on their heads; For glory, bright, they deck themselves.

+Geldner

Den Blitz in der Hand, glorreich, - im Haupte die goldenen Zahnreihen - bemalen sich die Schmucken zur Sch├╢nheit.

+Grassmann

Die blitzbewehrten, himmlischen, die lichten setzten auf das Haupt Zur Zier die goldnen Helme sich.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬGlorified, (Maruts), by U┼Ыanas, when you approach from afar to the opening of the rainy (firmament),then (the dwellers on earth), like those in heaven, are clamorous through fear.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

U┼Ыanas: u┼Ыanas─Б k─Бvyenaс╣Ыс╣гiс╣З─Б st┼лyam─Бn─Бс╕е;

Or = u┼Ыan─Бs─Бс╕е, i.e. desiring worshipper, stotс╣Ыn k─Бmayam─Бn─Бс╕е;

Clamorous: dyaurna cakradad bhiy─Б = like heaven, calls out with fear

+Jamison Brereton

When you drove with U┼Ыan─Б from afar to the тАЬloins of the oxтАЭ [=Vala cave?],
like heaven it [=cave] roared with fear.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Like almost every verse involving U┼Ыan─Б, this one is quite obscure. On the morphology of the name, see my art. in Fs. Jasanoff; for the mythological background and development of U┼Ыan─Б, chap. 4 in my RV between Two Worlds. I take this verse as a disguised treatment of the Vala myth, with which U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya is associated elsewhere. P─Бda a is also found at I.130.9; there I take U┼Ыan─Б as an acc. of goal (or perhaps a gen. with a gapped тАШhouseтАЩ), while here I take it as an instr. As discussed in the Fs. Jasanoff article, the word u┼Ы├бn─Б behaves essentially like an indeclinable in the RV.

In my analysis the curious expression ukс╣гс╣З├│ r├бndhram тАЬthe loins of the oxтАЭ (on randhr├б- see Got┼Н 1985 [MSS 44] and EWA s.v.) is a reference to the Vala cave: the loins are a weak or vulnerable spot in animals, and MIA randha- тАШopening, cleft, weak spotтАЩ shows how easily this can develop into a word that might qualify a cave.

A similar circumlocution for the Vala cave is n├бme g├│с╕е тАЬin the bend of the cowтАЭ (III.39.6). Geldner takes the phrase instead as a personal name; as he points out Ukс╣гс╣Зo Randhra is a PN in PB 13.9.19/JB III.150 and has the epithet k─Бvya-, apropos of the so-called Aukс╣гс╣Зorandhra S─Бman, but this is surely a secondary reinterpretation of this opaque vs. The roaring in c is the noise of the cows penned inside the cave.

Note the phonetic echo in the initial words of the first two p─Бdas: #u┼Ыan─Б #ukс╣гс╣Зas.

+Griffith

When eagerly ye from far away came to the cavern of the Bull,
He bellowed in his fear like Heaven.

+Macdonell

When eagerly from far ye came Nigh to the cavern of the bull, With fear, like Heaven, he roared aloud.

+Geldner

Als ihr mit Usanas zu Uksno Randhra aus der Ferne kamt, da br├╝llte er aus Furcht wie der Himmel donnert.

+Grassmann

Als ihr von Ferne voll Begier in das Versteck des Stieres drangt, Schrie, wie der Himmel, er vor Furcht.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen the spotted antelope or the swift tawny deer conveys them in their chariot, then the brilliant(Maruts) depart, and the rains have gone.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Riс╣Зan = as they flow in every direction, sarvatra pravahanti

+Jamison Brereton

When the chestnut side-horse guides the dappled (mares yoked) to their chariot,
the resplendent ones drive; they let flow the waters.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

pr├бс╣гс╣нi- тАШside-horseтАЩ is a rare word in the RV, occurring two other times in addition to a single instance of the deriv. pr├бс╣гс╣нimant-. As often, the occurrence of a rare word can be attributed to phonological triggers; here prс╣г╠е╠Б at─л r├бthe / pr├бс╣гс╣нir …

r├│hitaс╕е (with a nice scrambling of th ├а h…t in r├бthe тАж r├│hitaс╕е). Our p─Бda b is also found at I.39.6b, with r├бtheс╣гu pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гat─лr in the preceding p─Бda. (The other two occurrences are less phonologically driven.) The exact arrangement of the horses isnтАЩt clear, and the sandhi form pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гat─л has accordingly received different grammatical analyses. I take it as representing underlying pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гat─лс╕е, an acc. pl. fem., obj. of v├бhati (so also Grassmann, Bloomfield). Geldner (/Renou) seems to take it rather as a nom. pl. implicitly conjoined with r├│hitaс╕е, presumably with the verb agreeing with the latter. Hoffmann (Inj. 126) take the form as a dual nom., a parallel subj. to r├│hitaс╕е.

Oldenberg suggests that riс╣З├бn(n) is a nom. sg. participle, modifying the subjects of y─Б╠Бnti with incongruence of number. This seems unnecessary, since it can easily be a 3rd pl. injunctive, requiring no such grammatical adjustment.

+Griffith

When the red leader draws along their spotted deer yoked to the car.
The Bright Ones come, and shed the rain.

+Macdonell

When the red leader in their car The spotted deer directs, the bright Gods go: may they the waters free.

+Geldner

Wenn an ihrem Wagen die Schecken und der Rotfuchs als Beipferd ziehen, so fahren die Schmucken aus und lassen die Wasser laufen.

+Grassmann

Wenn nun ihr rothes Seitenpferd am Wagen beide Hirsche lenkt, So fahren hell sie, Wasser rinnt.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen was it, Maruts, who are gratified by praise, that you really deserted Indra? Who is there thatenjoys your friendship?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Deserted Indra?: i.e. they never deserted him, but alone of the gods stood by him in hisconflict with Vс╣Ыtra. Indra dispersed the clouds with his allies, the winds. Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 3.20; 12.8: Indradesired the gods to follow him, which they did. When Vс╣Ыtra breathed uponthem, they all ran away except theMaruts. They remained, encouraging Indra, saying: prahara bhagavo jahi v─лrayasva = strike, lord, kill, showyourself a hero

+Jamison Brereton

What is this now, you fair-weather friends?!тАФsince you have deserted Indra, who vaunts himself on partnership with you?

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On kadhapriyaс╕е see comm. ad I.30.20. Note k├бd dha тАж kadha-.

The verse seems to allude to the MarutsтАЩ supposed leaving Indra in the lurch at the Vс╣Ыtra battle, but this seems to be a slander: it is often said that they were the only gods who stayed with him (though Geldner adduces ┼ЪB IV.3.3.6, where they temporarily withdraw until Indra offers them a joint share of the sacrifice [7ff.].).

Certainly 24c expresses their help to Indra at that time.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(Their horses), quickly traversing (space), bear them travelling through the firmament, giving food to theworshipper.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Traveling crosswise the birds guide (the Maruts) here, as they [=Maruts] fly through the midspace.
(The Maruts) establish vital energy for their praiser.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the final word of the vs., v├бyaс╕е, as a pun, both nom. pl. тАШbirdsтАЩ and neut. acc. sg. тАШvital energyтАЩ, with the birds subject of vahanti in p─Бda a. Birds figure in several nearby hymns (VIII.3.23, 5.33), with the latter passage esp. close: … v─Бm …

v├бyo vahantu parс╣З├нnaс╕е тАЬLet your feathered birds [=horses] convey you two [=A┼Ыvins] here.тАЭ Geldner instead takes the obj. of vahanti here to be the MarutsтАЩ horses (supplied), with the Maruts themselves presumably the subj. Scarlatta (415-16) has the Maruts as subj. and clouds as obj., but in the absence of any clouds in the context, it seems better not to invent them. The disadvantage to my proposal is that the тАШbirdsтАЩ reading of v├бyaс╕е has to leap backwards over a nominal clause (dh─Б╠Бt─Бra stuvat├й тАж) that clearly has the Maruts as its nominal referent. Nonetheless, I think this kind of syntactic manipulation is possible in punning: the audience reaches the end of the verse and realizes that тАШbirdsтАЩ is the subject they were missing at the beginning, while also interpretating v├бyaс╕е as the neut. object of dh─Б╠Бt─Бraс╕е.

I am tempted to take dh─Б╠Бt─Бraс╕е as a periphrastic future: тАЬthey will establish тАжтАЭ

+Griffith

The man who lauds them strength and life.

+Macdonell

Their steeds that have a transverse course, Convey them flying through the air, To him that lauds them giving strength.

+Geldner

Kreuz und quer fahrend, lenken sie die durch die Luft fliegenden Rosse, indem sie dem S├дnger Kraft bringen.

+Grassmann

In schr├дgem Schusse fahren sie hinfliegend durch die weite Luft, Dass sie dem S├дnger Schatz verleihn.

+Elizarenkova

рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрд╣рд┐ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдЦрд▓реБ рдЕрд░реНрдЪрд┐рд╖рд╛ рддреЗрдЬрд╕рд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рдореБрдЦреНрдпрдГ рдЬрд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрдЬрд╛рдпрдд ред тАШ рджреАрдкрдЬрди (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рей. рез. ремрез) рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдХрд░реНрддрд░рд┐ рд▓реБрдЩрд┐ рдЪреНрд▓реЗрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдгрд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдЫрдиреНрджрдГ рдЙрдкрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрджрдиреАрдпрдГ рд╕реВрд░рдГ рди рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЗрд╡ред рддрджрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рддреЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрдЧреБрдгрд╛ рдорд░реБрддрдГ рднрд╛рдиреБрднрд┐рдГ рджреАрдкреНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╡рд┐ рддрд╕реНрдерд┐рд░реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдорд╡рддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддреЗ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдорд╛рд░реБрддреЗ рд╣реНрдпрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрддреЗ рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рдиреНрдорд░реБрддрдГ ред рддрджрдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛ рдЪ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛрддреНрддрд░рдпреЛрд░рд░реНрдзрд░реНрдЪрдпреЛрдГ рдХреНрд░рдореЗрдгрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрдорд░реБрддрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рее рее реирек рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAgni was born the first among the gods, like the brilliant sun in splendour; then they (the Maruts) stoodround in their radiance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The reference is to the ceremony called ─Аgnim─Бruta, when Agni is first worshipped,then the Maruts;

Brilliang: chandas = upacchandan─лya, the adorable

+Jamison Brereton

Since age-old Agni has (just) been born, like a metrical verse, with the ray of the sun,
they [=Maruts] have extended themselves with its radiant beams.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b contains two ambiguous forms, whose variant interpretations have produced very different tr.: ch├бndaс╕е may be nom. sg. masc. to ch├бnda- тАШpleasingтАЩ (if that stem exists; the only other possible ex. in the RV is at I.92.6, q.v.) or nom./acc. sg. neut. to ch├бndas- тАШmeterтАЩ; s┼л╠Бraс╕е can be nom. sg. masc. s┼л╠Бra- ‘sun’ or gen. sg.

sv├аr- ‘id.’ The standard tr. opt for the former choice in both cases, e.g., Renou тАЬtel un charmeur est le soleil, de par (son) ├йclat.тАЭ I have chosen the latter in both cases. The verse is a reference to the ritual here-and-now, the kindling of the fire at dawn: the phrase s┼л╠Бro arc├нс╣г─Б тАЬwith the ray of the sunтАЭ is an indicator of that time. I take ch├бndaс╕е as a metrical verse because the hymn opened with a similar metrical expression: triс╣гс╣н├║bham ├нс╣гam (see comm. ad vs. 1). The Maruts are characterized as chandast├║bh- тАШchanting in rhythmтАЩ in V.52.12, a cmpd that unites the chandas- of our vs. 36 with the 2nd part of triс╣гс╣н├║bh- in vs. 1. To be born тАЬlike a metrical verseтАЭ makes sense in a RVic context: the fire is kindled (born) as the verbal portion of the ritual begins to be spoken (born).

+Griffith

Agni was born the first of all, like Surya lovely with his light:
With lustre these have spread abroad.

+Macdonell

The ancient Agni has been born With brilliance like the shining sun; They with their beams spread far and wide.

+Geldner

Denn Agni ward als erster geboren; wie ein Verf├╝hrer lacht die Sonne im Strahlen-glanz. Zugleich mit den Sonnenstrahlen haben sie sich zerstreut.

+Grassmann

Denn Feuer ward zuerst erzeugt, erstrahlend wie mit Sonnenglanz; Sie brachen auf mit hellem Licht.

+Elizarenkova
